  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1525433298" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1525433298" />
    <a title="Borum" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/15410264-borum"><img alt="Borum" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1562163411p2/15410264.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1525433298?book_show_action=true">Jan 25, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Borum" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Borum" href="/user/show/15410264-borum">Borum</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/22428801-six-characters-in-search-of-an-author">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1525433298" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13007932861839647358">A while back, when I made an attempt at creative writing, all the characters in my story seemed to be full of possibilities at first, and then became more and more willful and awry as the story progressed. I blamed this on my lack of foreplanning and writing experience, and usually just abandoned my creations that turned out like the unanticipated Frankenstein. <br/><br/>I got a similar feeling when I was acting or directing in our college drama club. At first reading, I'm clueless to what's facing me but</span>
  <span id="freeText13007932861839647358" style="display:none">A while back, when I made an attempt at creative writing, all the characters in my story seemed to be full of possibilities at first, and then became more and more willful and awry as the story progressed. I blamed this on my lack of foreplanning and writing experience, and usually just abandoned my creations that turned out like the unanticipated Frankenstein. <br /><br />I got a similar feeling when I was acting or directing in our college drama club. At first reading, I'm clueless to what's facing me but when I (or the actors that I'm directing) put our voice and gestures into those blank words, the characters all turn out to be something quite unexpected with a life of its own. This was aggravated by the fact that the characters were interpreted in different angles by each of the actors, the director, and the prop team (and possibly by the author if the author could have been present in our amateur drama club). Had it not been a collective effort, I would have gladly given up on the project (good riddance to you all!) and resorted to a solitary internal reenactment of my own version of the play. Alas, the show must go on, and I was forced to be molded into someone else's idea of the drama.<br /><br />I was also unsettled by my first performing experience, or rather the end of my first performance. After about an hour of being an avatar of someone else's figment of imagination, the curtain closed down on us with the lights slowly fading away. As I stepped up to bow to the audience, I had the strangest sensation of being deserted by the character that remained and lived on in the play while I became the empty shell, or a dream or a ghost of the character instead of the other way around. <br /><br />As I read and then watched the play of Pirandello, I was reminded of the aforementioned personal impressions of drama (and I was just an amateur with not even a hint of method acting in me!) and I couldn't help sympathizing with both the characters and the director (manager). This meta-drama delves through the metaphysical elements of theatre and fantasy by reversing the roles of both the creatr and created, the actors and the characters, and finds the common ground between our fantasy and reality, as stated in the play: "nature uses the instrument of human fantasy in order to pursue her high creative purpose." <br /><br />This common ground, which is called 'absurdity' is made explicit many times in the play by the characters' argument in that the actors are no more real than the characters themselves and that reality is no less absurd or plausible than what is on stage: "... you know well that life is full of infinite absudities, which strangely enough, do not even need to appear plausible, since they are true."<br /><br />The multifaceted existence of the characters also points out the clashes between different interpretations and between people in reality. It also reminded me of my past frictions in the drama club and in my real life as well: <br /><br />"how can we ever come to an understanding if I put in the words I utter the sense and value of things as I see them; while you who listen to me must inevitably translate them according to the conception of things each one of you has within himself"<br /><br />"We believe this conscience to be a single thing, but it is many-sided. There is one for this person, and another for that."<br /><br />"It is merely to show you that one is born to life in many forms, in many shapes, as tree, or as stone, as water, as butterfly, or as woman. So one may also born a character in a play."<br /><br />Thus the characters reveal both our limitations in communication and Pirandello sometimes use this misunderstanding as comic relief: "Is it my fault if France won't send us any more good comedies, and we are reduced to putting on Pirandello's works, where nobody understands anything, and where the author plays the fool with us all?"<br /><br />However, even after the release of self-derisive wit, the audience is reminded again by the characters of the cruelty of this 'game of art' which is for them their 'sole reality'. Susan Sontag's 'Regarding the Pain of Others' was a jab at the secondary violence of the representation of violence. Is Pirandello warning against the inured and desensitized audience to the painful reality behind the seeming illusion of drama, and beseeching for their awareness of the 'real' suffering and tragedy beneath the facade of comedy?<br /><br />"I feel what I think; and I seem to be philosophizing only for those who do not think what they feel"<br /><br />"For man never reasons so much and becomes so introspective as when he suffers."<br /><br />However the interpretation or reenactment of the characters end up, the characters seem to have an endless fate (or will) that is independent of the author, the actor or the director and live on after the lights are dimmed and the curtains drop. This feeling haunted me long after I stopped acting and I got caught up in these two lines where the characters at first asked the manager to live only for a moment in the actors, but then eventually turns the table around to reveal the ephemeral and fragile existence of our own 'reality'.<br /><br />The Father: We want to live.<br />The Manager (ironically): For Eternity?<br />The Father: No, sir, only for a moment.... in you.<br /><br />The Father: Ours is an immutable reality which should make you shudder when you approach us if you are really conscious of the fact that your reality is a mere transitory and fleeting illusion, taking this form today and that tomorrow.<br /><br />Another line put me on a guilt trip as I remembered all those stories and characters I rejected in the end. If we, too, are a creation of God, are we also as willful and yet helpless to change our own fate?<br /><br />"When a character is born, he acquires at once such an independence, even of his own author, that he can be imagined by everybody even in many other situations where the author never dreamed of placing him; and so he acquires for himself a meaning which the author never thought of giving him.<br /><br />.... Imagine such a misfortune for characters as I have described to you: to be born of an author's fantasy, and be denied life by him; and then answer me if these characters left alive, and yet without life, weren't right in doing what they did do and are doing now, after they have attempted everything in their power to persuade him to give them their stage life."<br /><br />Although I liked existentialist novels by Camus and Sartre, I never really enjoyed Beckett's absurdist play 'Waiting for Godot'. Maybe it was because I haven't had enough of both the stage of life and theatre (I was in highschool). I certainly appreciated Pirandello's play both in book and on screen. Some charitable soul uploaded this BBC production on youtube, and the performances are marvelous.<br /><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://youtu.be/WvWCfIYPZK0?list=PLPxTfzeDGPUu-3GE0VD7Hqx8KwItGyu1W">https://youtu.be/WvWCfIYPZK0?list=PLP...</a><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://youtu.be/I_FV4-BM9IA?list=PLPxTfzeDGPUu-3GE0VD7Hqx8KwItGyu1W">https://youtu.be/I_FV4-BM9IA?list=PLP...</a><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://youtu.be/1gwDorSE8pg?list=PLPxTfzeDGPUu-3GE0VD7Hqx8KwItGyu1W">https://youtu.be/1gwDorSE8pg?list=PLP...</a><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://youtu.be/R_ygc3UGo6g?list=PLPxTfzeDGPUu-3GE0VD7Hqx8KwItGyu1W">https://youtu.be/R_ygc3UGo6g?list=PLP...</a><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://youtu.be/nfUuTZjG3kI?list=PLPxTfzeDGPUu-3GE0VD7Hqx8KwItGyu1W">https://youtu.be/nfUuTZjG3kI?list=PLP...</a><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://youtu.be/0lr8Mjx1IAE?list=PLPxTfzeDGPUu-3GE0VD7Hqx8KwItGyu1W">https://youtu.be/0lr8Mjx1IAE?list=PLP...</a><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://youtu.be/CjZfQk047oI?list=PLPxTfzeDGPUu-3GE0VD7Hqx8KwItGyu1W">https://youtu.be/CjZfQk047oI?list=PLP...</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="13007932861839647358" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2828422984" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5742316838823231040">😮😮😮<br/>What did I just read???<br/>This play is my pick for 1921 for #192019challenge and though the adaptation I got is modern, the spirit comes through.<br/><br/>A company of actors is practicing a play, when 6 people come in. They say they are characters left unfinished by their author, and they’re looking to set their story down.<br/>The actors oblige them.<br/><br/>What ensues is a whirlwind of mindf$&!ery that shows the shadow side of creation.<br/>I’d love to see this done live.</span>
  <span id="freeText5742316838823231040" style="display:none">😮😮😮<br />What did I just read???<br />This play is my pick for 1921 for #192019challenge and though the adaptation I got is modern, the spirit comes through.<br /><br />A company of actors is practicing a play, when 6 people come in. They say they are characters left unfinished by their author, and they’re looking to set their story down.<br />The actors oblige them.<br /><br />What ensues is a whirlwind of mindf$&amp;!ery that shows the shadow side of creation.<br />I’d love to see this done live.</span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3354272395" />
    <a title="Suha" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/33599214-suha"><img alt="Suha" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1407013913p2/33599214.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3354272395?book_show_action=true">May 25, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Suha" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Suha" href="/user/show/33599214-suha">Suha</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3354272395" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3755915672887187850">Salted and caramelized delicious nuts. This is one of the most entertaining and creative short reads Ive encountered. <br/><br/>This is about a family of 6 mysterious strangers that appear in the theater while interrupting rehearsal of a play. They tell the director and the cast that they are made for a play but the author didn’t write down the plot. As a result, they are stuck in the forever present unless the director is convinced to stage/write their drama. <br/><br/>Before they showed up, the director of the pl</span>
  <span id="freeText3755915672887187850" style="display:none">Salted and caramelized delicious nuts. This is one of the most entertaining and creative short reads Ive encountered. <br /><br />This is about a family of 6 mysterious strangers that appear in the theater while interrupting rehearsal of a play. They tell the director and the cast that they are made for a play but the author didn’t write down the plot. As a result, they are stuck in the forever present unless the director is convinced to stage/write their drama. <br /><br />Before they showed up, the director of the play was complaining that the current plot which is another Pirandello play, isn’t good enough and lacks necessary drama and now “we are reduced to staging words by Pirandello. To those who understands them, bravo.”<br /><br />The father of the family of strangers tries to convince the present actors that he and his family are just born characters, however the author who created them did not write their story, therefore they are in search of an author. The entire team of actors think that what the father said was insane, but the father straightens it by saying that he and his family were born characters just like some are born animals or humans or plants. <br />Yet the cast still thinks it is absurd “. . . life is full of infinite absurdities, which strangely enough, do not even need to appear plausible since they are true.” But the father insists that they have to be played, this is what they are made for! <br />Other than well written, I personally found the play to be very amusing yet powerful. The concepts of destiny, fate, reality and existence, all came to mind while reading. This is a 1 sitting read, so go ahead and read it 😊 it’s good. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="3755915672887187850" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_121327923" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/121327923" />
    <a title="Trisha" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4280826-trisha"><img alt="Trisha" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1585779037p2/4280826.jpg" /></a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Trisha" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Trisha" href="/user/show/4280826-trisha">Trisha</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer121327923" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11950794649364975090">I really enjoyed this satirical, twisting look at theatre and the nature of reality. The characters each have competing views of the reality of their drama, just as people in real life have differing views of the same event. The play-within-a-play staging sets up a self-referentiality that I found at once thought-provoking and hilarious. A wonderful play that I highly recommend.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2679604598" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

    <a title="Alen Piralić" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/92365056-alen-pirali"><img alt="Alen Piralić" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1596905816p2/92365056.jpg" /></a>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2679604598?book_show_action=true">Jul 26, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alen Piralić" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alen Piralić" href="/user/show/92365056-alen-pirali">Alen Piralić</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">philosophy lovers</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/92365056-alen-pirali?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/92365056-alen-pirali?shelf=drame">drame</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2679604598" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17041562416270898756">Pirandello's masterpiece. He discusses the idea and function of the theaters and plays through a play! A brilliant mind. Deliberately or not, he definitely made it very difficult, maybe even impossible, for theater directors, and actors, to embody this work.<br/><br/>With many contrasts, but such an ease, he brings up to the scene dark and overwhelming questions about human nature, the meaning of life and human stupidity and hypocrisy - his character quotes make you anxious, they make you question reality</span>
  <span id="freeText17041562416270898756" style="display:none">Pirandello's masterpiece. He discusses the idea and function of the theaters and plays through a play! A brilliant mind. Deliberately or not, he definitely made it very difficult, maybe even impossible, for theater directors, and actors, to embody this work.<br /><br />With many contrasts, but such an ease, he brings up to the scene dark and overwhelming questions about human nature, the meaning of life and human stupidity and hypocrisy - his character quotes make you anxious, they make you question reality and the way you coped with world and life so far. <br /><br />His characters, the way I see it, are trying to, through elaboration of their misery, tell us, point it out for us - I can hear them scream it so vividly - that we no longer know how to live in reality, that we have forgotten to be present in the most important, those essential moments of our todays; they are trying to warn us that we think and debate about something not real, what is only a play, an illusion, with so much more interest compared to what really is real - tragedies of life that are now and here!<br />And that is true misery - not so much their, in the end, but ours.<br /><br />*hrvatski<br /><br />Pirandello, pripremajući ovu svoju dramu, kao da se narugao svim glumcima i kazališnim redateljima koji će ovo njegovo remek-djelo pokušati utjeloviti - utjeloviti ga, to znači pokvariti ga, nagrditi ga izmjenama i previdima; utjeloviti ga, to je nemoguće.<br /><br />Zanimljiv je način na koji Pirandello problematizira ulogu kazališta i njegov utjecaj na društvo uopće, njegovo mjesto u europskoj kulturi, odnosno ulogu u životu suvremenog čovjeka, a to čini sa takvom suptilnosti da, iako lansira i to veliko pitanje, nimalo ne zasjenjuje glavnu ideju ove drame.<br /><br />Pirandello stavlja svog deus ex machina na početak, dovodeći na kazališne daske, pod svjetlo reflektora, likove koji prekidaju pomalo učmalu, ali prije svega plitku i makinalnu svakodnevicu kazališnog biološkog inventara. Isprva nelogičnošću svoje pojave, a kasnije dramatičnošću svojih života i dubinom ideja, poruka koje iznose, Pirandellovi likovi dovode sve u pitanje - ne samo kazalište, već i smisao ljudskog postojanja, brak, spolne odnose, obiteljske odnose kao paradigmu međuljudskih odnosa, ljudsku prirodu i ljudsko ponašanje, odnosno motive ponašanja. U njihovom diskursu nema tabua, u pitanje su dovodeni svetost života, ljudsko dostojanstvo, autentičnost čovjeka kao pojedinca, tančine njegova bića, crninu, ali ne fizičku, već metafizičku, koja ga tlači i pribija stiješnjena uza zid i ne da mu disati; pod lupu likovi stavljaju metafiziku čovjeka, koja, što svjedoče svojim životima, čovjeku ne da živjeti.<br /><br />Gore spomenute elemente pisac iznosi tek u obliku pitanja ili ukaza, i ne bavi se dublje njima. Međutim, ono na čemu inzistira, odnosno na čemu inzistiraju likovi, ono zbog čega je i nastalo djelo, je potreba, žudnja da ih se utjelovi, da se utjelove i ispričaju njihove životne priče dajući im slobodu nastupanja, poklanjajući im taj dar pažnje, slušajući ih i suosjećajući - ono što svako ljudsko biće želi da mu drugi daju.<br /><br />Konačno, to najvažnije, ta Pirandellova opomena svima nama, vjerojatno iznikla iz autorove ogorčenosti ljudskim licemjerjem i cinizmom, može se razumjeti iz sljedećeg Očevog citata: ''Ali oprostite molim vas! Zašto želite pokvariti, u ime nekakve vulgarne, činjenične istine, ovo čudo zbilje koje se rađa prizvana, privučena, uobličen samom scenom i mnogo istinitija od vas?''.<br />Kritika je, dakle, upućena svima onima, koji zbog primitivnih, uopće nečovječnih pobuda vlastitih ega zatomljuju ili izopačuju istinu kako ih ne bi zasjenila, onima koji, u ime nekakve vulgarne, otuđene, unakažene, osakaćene istine, anti-istine, zatajuju jedinu istinu koja jest, možda zato da ih ne prokaže, pa se onda sažalijevamo nad kazališnim komadima, raspredamo o tragičnosti radnje koju prikazuju, o nesretnim, nezasluženo nepravednim sudbinama koje glumci prikazuju, a istovremeno od stvarnih tragedija, kojima smo i sami možda uzroci, ili barem susjedi i prijatelji, možda čak i nadređeni, oni u poziciji, koji imaju vlast život zagorčati ili zasladiti, okrećemo glave, odričući im pravo da budu. <br /><br />Još jednom, genijalno, daleko, daleko ispred vremena, iznad mozgova, iznad gubica i guzica.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17041562416270898756" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3066515349" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3066515349" />
    <a title="IrritableSatirist" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/97478957-irritablesatirist"><img alt="IrritableSatirist" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1558304794p2/97478957.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3066515349?book_show_action=true">Dec 31, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="IrritableSatirist" class="user" itemprop="url" name="IrritableSatirist" href="/user/show/97478957-irritablesatirist">IrritableSatirist</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780451526885" href="/book/show/540665.Six_Characters_in_Search_of_an_Author">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/97478957-irritablesatirist?shelf=reviews">reviews</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3066515349" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1161269556077190435">This has an amazing premise with lots of potential, but Luigi Pirandello failed to develop a narrative to explore it. What little plot exists in <i>Six Characters in Search of an Author</i> is not enough to maintain interest through the entire work. It is a phenomenal premise squandered.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('tCuqeL1mVg8QonTNzBGrzMb/9ri+hpaYNLA9ddRt/z4e8CJNhlaLvulK2C5KwDahJroXpg4qWR4mA7eXjCbCSw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('u7ePbYJYVe2W3fu5z7Oq6uskC/VSNnPSTdh42+2Pd90RbAdYuWiIXG81V1pJYjeHC2Hq6+KavFRfa/I5tcRKqA==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

Set in the seventeenth century, the play follows Anna Fierling -- &quot;Mother Courage&quot; -- an itinerant trader, as she pulls her wagon of wares and her children through the blood and carnage of Europe\'s religious wars. Battered by hardships, brutality, and the degradation and death of her children, she ultimately finds herself alone with the one thing in which she truly believes -- her ramshackle wagon with its tattered flag and freight of boots and brandy. Fitting herself in its harness, the old woman manages, with the last of her strength, to drag it onward to the next battle. Here are Zeno’s interminable attempts to quit smoking, his courtship of the beautiful yet unresponsive Ada, his unexpected–and unexpectedly happy–marriage to Ada’s homely sister Augusta, and his affair with a shrill-voiced aspiring singer. More than any other dramatist, O\'Neill introduced American drama to the dramatic realism pioneered by Russian playwright Anton Chekhov, Norwegian playwright Henrik Ib<\/span>\n  <span id=\"freeText1519645048623952224\" style=\"display:none\">Eugene Gladstone O\'Neill (1888-1953) was a Nobel prize winning American playwright. More than any other dramatist, O\'Neill introduced American drama to the dramatic realism pioneered by Russian playwright Anton Chekhov, Norwegian playwright Henrik Ibsen, and Swedish playwright August Strindberg, and was the first to use true American vernacular in his speeches. His plays involve characters who inhabit the fringes of society, engaging in depraved behaviour, where they struggle to maintain their hopes and aspirations but ultimately slide into disillusionment and despair. O\'Neill wrote only one comedy Ah, Wilderness!, all his other plays involve some degree of tragedy and personal pessimism. O\'Neill\'s first published play, Beyond the Horizon, opened on Broadway in 1920 to great acclaim, and was awarded the Pulitzer Prize for Drama. His best-known plays include Anna Christie (Pulitzer Prize 1922), The First Man (1922), and The Hairy Ape (1922). In 1936 he received the Nobel Prize for Literature.<\/span>\n  <a data-text-id=\"1519645048623952224\" href=\"#\" onclick=\"swapContent(\$(this));; return false;\">...more<\/a>\n\n    <\/div>\n\n       <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/7702.Luigi_Pirandello">About Luigi Pirandello</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/7702.Luigi_Pirandello"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1464208347p3/7702.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/7702.Luigi_Pirandello">Luigi Pirandello
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__followerCount'>
911
followers
</div>

</div>
</div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer4587487811291381274">Luigi Pirandello; Agrigento 28 June 1867 – Rome 10 December 1936) was an Italian dramatist, novelist, poet, and short story writer whose greatest contributions were his plays. <br/>He was awarded the 1934 Nobel Prize in Literature for "his almost magical power to turn psychological analysis into good theatre. <br/>Pirandello's works include novels, hundreds of short stories, and about 40 plays, some of whic</span>
  <span id="freeText4587487811291381274" style="display:none">Luigi Pirandello; Agrigento 28 June 1867 – Rome 10 December 1936) was an Italian dramatist, novelist, poet, and short story writer whose greatest contributions were his plays. <br />He was awarded the 1934 Nobel Prize in Literature for "his almost magical power to turn psychological analysis into good theatre. <br />Pirandello's works include novels, hundreds of short stories, and about 40 plays, some of which are written in Sicilian. Pirandello's tragic farces are often seen as forerunners of the Theatre of the Absurd.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4587487811291381274" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
</div>

<div class="clear"></div></div></div><div class="bigBoxBottom"></div></div>

      <div class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/work/quotes/15468851-sei-personaggi-in-cerca-d-autore">Quotes from Six Characters in...</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">

            <span class="readable">&ldquo;Life is full of strange absurdities, which, strangely enough, do not even need to appear plausible, since they are true.&rdquo;</span>
            <nobr>
              &mdash;
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/quotes/484675-life-is-full-of-strange-absurdities-which-strangely-enough-do">1059 likes</a>
            </nobr>
            <div class="clear"></div>
          </div>
          <div class="stacked" tyle="padding-bottom:15px">
            <span class="readable">&ldquo;THE FATHER: But don't you see that the whole trouble lies here? In words, words. Each one of us has within him a whole world of things, each man of us his own special world. And how can we ever come to an understanding if I put in the words I utter the sense and value of things as I see them; while you who listen to me must inevitably translate them according to the conception of things each one of you has within himself. We think we understand each other, but we never really do.&rdquo;</span>
            <nobr>
              &mdash;
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/quotes/8649-the-father-but-don-t-you-see-that-the-whole-trouble">111 likes</a>
